<div class="NavHead" style="font-size: 105%; background: transparent; text-align: left;">List of MPs</div>
<ul class="NavContent" style="list-style: none none; margin-left: 0; text-align:left;display:none; font-size: 105%; margin-top: 0; margin-bottom: 0; line-height: inherit;"><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"><a href="/wiki/Rachael_Maskell" title="Rachael Maskell">Rachael Maskell</a> (<a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">L</a>)</li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"><a href="/wiki/Julian_Sturdy" title="Julian Sturdy">Julian Sturdy</a> (<a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">C</a>)</li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_and_the_Humber_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="Yorkshire and the Humber (European Parliament constituency)">Yorkshire and the Humber</a></td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row">Website</th><td><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.york.gov.uk/">york.gov.uk</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>York</b> is a <a href="/wiki/City_status_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="City status in the United Kingdom">city</a> and <a href="/wiki/Unitary_authority" title="Unitary authority">unitary authority area</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_Yorkshire" title="North Yorkshire">North Yorkshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, the population of the council area which includes nearby villages was 208,200 as of 2017<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and the population of the Urban area was 153,717 at the 2011 census. Located at the confluence of the Rivers <a href="/wiki/River_Ouse,_Yorkshire" title="River Ouse, Yorkshire">Ouse</a> and <a href="/wiki/River_Foss" title="River Foss">Foss</a>, it is the <a href="/wiki/County_town" title="County town">county town</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Historic_counties_of_England" title="Historic counties of England">historic county</a> of <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire" title="Yorkshire">Yorkshire</a>. The city is known for its famous historical landmarks such as <a href="/wiki/York_Minster" title="York Minster">York Minster</a> and the <a href="/wiki/York_city_walls" title="York city walls">city walls</a>, as well as a variety of cultural and sporting activities, which makes it a popular tourist destination in England. The <a href="/wiki/Local_authority" class="mw-redirect" title="Local authority">local authority</a> is the <a href="/wiki/City_of_York_Council" title="City of York Council">City of York Council</a>, a single tier governing body responsible for providing all local services and facilities throughout the city. The <b>City of York</b> local government district includes rural areas beyond the old city boundaries. It is about 20 miles north-east of <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a>.
</p><p>The city was founded by the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Britain" title="Roman Britain">Romans</a> as <a href="/wiki/Eboracum" title="Eboracum">Eboracum</a> in 71&#160;AD. It became the capital of the Roman province of <a href="/wiki/Britannia_Inferior" title="Britannia Inferior">Britannia Inferior</a>, and later of the kingdoms of <a href="/wiki/Deira" title="Deira">Deira</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northumbria" class="mw-redirect" title="Northumbria">Northumbria</a> and <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B3rv%C3%ADk" class="mw-redirect" title="Jórvík">Jórvík</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, York grew as a major wool trading centre and became the capital of the northern <a href="/wiki/Ecclesiastical_province" title="Ecclesiastical province">ecclesiastical province</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a>, a role it has retained.<sup id="cite_ref-timeline_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timeline-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> In the 19th century, York became a major hub of the railway network and a confectionery manufacturing centre, a status it maintained well into the 20th century. During the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, York was bombed as part of the <a href="/wiki/Baedeker_Blitz" title="Baedeker Blitz">Baedeker Blitz</a>. Although less affected by bombing than other northern cities, several historic buildings were gutted and restoration efforts continued into the 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> In 2000, York suffered very severe flooding as the River Ouse rose, affecting over 300 homes.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The economy of York is dominated by services. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_York" title="University of York">University of York</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_Health_Service" title="National Health Service">National Health Service</a> are major employers, whilst tourism has become an important element of the local economy. In 2016, York became <a href="/wiki/Sister_city" title="Sister city">sister cities</a> with the Chinese city of <a href="/wiki/Nanjing" title="Nanjing">Nanjing</a>, as per an agreement signed by the <a href="/wiki/Lord_Mayor_of_York" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Mayor of York">Lord Mayor of York</a>, focusing on building links in tourism, education, science, technology and culture.<sup id="cite_ref-York_Press_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-York_Press-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Visit_York_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Visit_York-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Today, the city is a popular tourist attraction, especially for international visitors from China and Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> In 2017, York became UK's first human rights city, which formalised the city’s aim to use human rights in decision making.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_York" title="History of York">History of York</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origin_of_the_name">Origin of the name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Origin of the name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The word <i>York</i> (Old Norse: <i><a href="/wiki/J%C3%B3rv%C3%ADk" class="mw-redirect" title="Jórvík">Jórvík</a></i>) is derived from the <a href="/wiki/Common_Brittonic" title="Common Brittonic">Brittonic</a> name <i>Eburākon</i> (<a href="/wiki/Latin_(language)" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin (language)">Latinised</a> variously as <i><a href="/wiki/Eboracum" title="Eboracum">Eboracum</a></i>, <i>Eburacum</i> or <i>Eburaci</i>),  a combination of <i>eburos</i> "yew-tree" (cf. Old Irish <i>ibar</i> "yew-tree" (Irish <i>iobhar, iubhar, iúr</i>, Gaelic <i>iubhar</i>), Welsh <i>efwr</i> "alder buckthorn", Breton <i>evor</i> "alder buckthorn") and a suffix of <a href="/wiki/Appurtenance" title="Appurtenance">appurtenance</a> <i>*-āko(n)</i> "belonging to-, place of-" (cf. Welsh <i>-og</i>)<sup id="cite_ref-Xavier_Delamarre_2003,_p._159_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xavier_Delamarre_2003,_p._159-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> meaning either "place of the <a href="/wiki/Taxus_baccata" title="Taxus baccata">yew</a> trees" (cf. <i>efrog</i> in <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh</a>, Old Irish <i>iubrach</i> "grove of yew trees, place with one or more yew trees", <i>iúrach</i> in <a href="/wiki/Irish_Gaelic" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Gaelic">Irish Gaelic</a> and <i>iùbhrach</i> in <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">Scottish Gaelic</a>; the city itself is called <i>Eabhrach</i> (Irish) and <i>Eabhraig</i> in those languages, from the Latin <i>Eboracum</i>); or alternatively, "the settlement of (a man named) <i>Eburos</i>" (a <a href="/wiki/Celtic_languages" title="Celtic languages">Celtic</a> personal name is mentioned in different documents as <i>Eβουρος</i>, <i>Eburus</i> and <i>Eburius</i> and, when combined with the Celtic possessive suffix <i>*-āko(n)</i>, could be used to denote his property).<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Xavier_Delamarre_2003,_p._159_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xavier_Delamarre_2003,_p._159-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The name <i>Eboracum</i> became the <a href="/wiki/Angles" title="Angles">Anglian</a> <i>Eoforwic</i> in the 7th&#160;century: a compound of <i>Eofor-</i>, from the old name, and <i>-wic</i> a village, probably by conflation of the element <i>Ebor-</i> with a <a href="/wiki/Germanic_languages" title="Germanic languages">Germanic</a> root <i>*eburaz</i> (boar); by the 7th&#160;century the <a href="/wiki/Old_English" title="Old English">Old English</a> for 'boar' had become <i>eofor</i>. When the <a href="/wiki/Danes_(Germanic_tribe)" title="Danes (Germanic tribe)">Danish</a> army conquered the city in 866, its name became <i>Jórvík</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-coyyh_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coyyh-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Old_French" title="Old French">Old French</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norman_language" title="Norman language">Norman</a> name of the city following the <a href="/wiki/Norman_conquest_of_England" title="Norman conquest of England">Norman Conquest</a> was recorded as "Everwic" (modern Norman "Évèroui") in works such as Wace's <a href="/wiki/Roman_de_Rou" title="Roman de Rou">Roman de Rou</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> <i>Jórvík</i>, meanwhile, gradually reduced to <i>York</i> in the centuries after the Conquest, moving from the <a href="/wiki/Middle_English" title="Middle English">Middle English</a> <i>Yerk</i> in the 14th&#160;century through <i>Yourke</i> in the 16th&#160;century to <i>Yarke</i> in the 17th&#160;century. The form <i>York</i> was first recorded in the 13th&#160;century.<sup id="cite_ref-timeline_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timeline-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Willis35_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Willis35-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Many company and place names, such as the Ebor race meeting, refer to the Latinised Brittonic, Roman name.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 12th‑century chronicler <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_of_Monmouth" title="Geoffrey of Monmouth">Geoffrey of Monmouth</a>, in his fictional account of the prehistoric kings of Britain, <i><i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/Historia_Regum_Britanniae" title="Historia Regum Britanniae">Historia Regum Britanniae</a></i></i>, suggests the name derives from that of a pre-Roman city founded by the legendary king <a href="/wiki/Ebraucus" title="Ebraucus">Ebraucus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_York" title="Archbishop of York">Archbishop of York</a> uses <i>Ebor</i> as his surname in his signature.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Roman_Fortifications_in_Museum_Gardens_York.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Roman_Fortifications_in_Museum_Gardens_York.jpg/220px-Roman_Fortifications_in_Museum_Gardens_York.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Roman_Fortifications_in_Museum_Gardens_York.jpg/330px-Roman_Fortifications_in_Museum_Gardens_York.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Roman_Fortifications_in_Museum_Gardens_York.jpg/440px-Roman_Fortifications_in_Museum_Gardens_York.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1632" data-file-height="1232" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Roman_Fortifications_in_Museum_Gardens_York.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Roman wall and the west corner tower of <a href="/wiki/Eboracum" title="Eboracum">Eboracum</a>. The top half is medieval.</div></div></div>
<p>Archaeological evidence suggests that <a href="/wiki/Mesolithic" title="Mesolithic">Mesolithic</a> people settled in the region of York between 8000 and 7000&#160;BC, although it is not known whether their settlements were permanent or temporary. By the time of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_conquest_of_Britain" title="Roman conquest of Britain">Roman conquest of Britain</a>, the area was occupied by a <a href="/wiki/Tribe" title="Tribe">tribe</a> known to the Romans as the <a href="/wiki/Brigantes" title="Brigantes">Brigantes</a>. The Brigantian tribal area initially became a Roman client state, but later its leaders became more hostile and the Roman <a href="/wiki/Legio_IX_Hispana" title="Legio IX Hispana">Ninth Legion</a> was sent north of the <a href="/wiki/Humber" title="Humber">Humber</a> into Brigantian territory.<sup id="cite_ref-Willis26_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Willis26-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The city was founded in 71&#160;AD, when the Ninth Legion conquered the Brigantes and constructed a wooden military <a href="/wiki/Castra" title="Castra">fortress</a> on flat ground above the <a href="/wiki/River_Ouse,_Yorkshire" title="River Ouse, Yorkshire">River Ouse</a> close to its <a href="/wiki/Confluence" title="Confluence">confluence</a> with the <a href="/wiki/River_Foss" title="River Foss">River Foss</a>. The fortress, whose walls were rebuilt in stone by the VI legion based there subsequent to the IX legion, covered an area of 50 acres (20&#160;ha) and was inhabited by 6,000 <a href="/wiki/Roman_legion" title="Roman legion">legionary</a> soldiers. The site of the <i>principia</i> (HQ) of the fortress lies under the foundations of <a href="/wiki/York_Minster" title="York Minster">York Minster</a>, and excavations in the undercroft have revealed part of the Roman structure and columns.<sup id="cite_ref-coyyh_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coyyh-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ytss-2_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ytss-2-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Constantine_York.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Constantine_York.jpg/190px-Constantine_York.jpg" decoding="async" width="190" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Constantine_York.jpg/285px-Constantine_York.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Constantine_York.jpg/380px-Constantine_York.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Constantine_York.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Statue_of_Constantine_the_Great,_York" title="Statue of Constantine the Great, York">Roman Emperor Constantine the Great proclaimed Emperor at York in 306&#160;AD</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The Emperors <a href="/wiki/Hadrian" title="Hadrian">Hadrian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Septimius_Severus" title="Septimius Severus">Septimius Severus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Constantius_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Constantius I">Constantius I</a> all held court in York during their various campaigns. During his stay 207–211&#160;AD, the Emperor Severus proclaimed York capital of the province of Britannia Inferior, and it is likely that it was he who granted York the privileges of a '<a href="/wiki/Colonia_(Roman)" title="Colonia (Roman)">colonia</a>' or city. Constantius I died in 306&#160;AD during his stay in York, and his son <a href="/wiki/Constantine_the_Great" title="Constantine the Great">Constantine the Great</a> was proclaimed Emperor by the troops based in the fortress.<sup id="cite_ref-ytss-2_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ytss-2-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> In 314&#160;AD a bishop from York attended the <a href="/wiki/Synod_of_Arles_(314)" class="mw-redirect" title="Synod of Arles (314)">Council at Arles</a> to represent Christians from the <a href="/wiki/Roman_province" title="Roman province">province</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While the Roman <i>colonia</i> and <a href="/wiki/Castra" title="Castra">fortress</a> were located on high ground, by 400&#160;AD the town was victim to occasional flooding from the Rivers Ouse and Foss, and the population reduced.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> York declined in the <a href="/wiki/Sub-Roman_Britain" title="Sub-Roman Britain">post-Roman</a> era, and was taken and settled by the <a href="/wiki/Angles" title="Angles">Angles</a> in the 5th&#160;century.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Reclamation of parts of the town was initiated in the 7th&#160;century under <a href="/wiki/Edwin_of_Northumbria" title="Edwin of Northumbria">King Edwin</a> of <a href="/wiki/Northumbria" class="mw-redirect" title="Northumbria">Northumbria</a>, and York became his chief city.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The first wooden  <a href="/wiki/Minster_(church)" title="Minster (church)">minster church</a> was built in York for the baptism of Edwin in 627, according to the Venerable Bede.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Edwin ordered the small wooden church be rebuilt in stone; however, he was killed in 633, and the task of completing the stone minster fell to his successor <a href="/wiki/Oswald_of_Northumbria" title="Oswald of Northumbria">Oswald</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-coyyh_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coyyh-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ymhist_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ymhist-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> In the following century, <a href="/wiki/Alcuin_of_York" class="mw-redirect" title="Alcuin of York">Alcuin of York</a> came to the cathedral school of York. He had a long career as a teacher and scholar, first at the school at York now known as <a href="/wiki/St_Peter%27s_School,_York" title="St Peter&#39;s School, York">St Peter's School</a>, founded in 627&#160;AD, and later as <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a>'s leading advisor on ecclesiastical and educational affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 866, Northumbria was in the midst of internecine struggles when the <a href="/wiki/Vikings" title="Vikings">Vikings</a> raided and captured York. Under Viking rule the city became a major river port, part of the extensive Viking trading routes throughout northern Europe. The last ruler of an independent Jórvík, <a href="/wiki/Eric_Bloodaxe" title="Eric Bloodaxe">Eric Bloodaxe</a>, was driven from the city in 954&#160;AD by King <a href="/wiki/Eadred" title="Eadred">Eadred</a> in his successful attempt to complete the unification of England.<sup id="cite_ref-coyyjv_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coyyjv-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="After_the_conquest">After the conquest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: After the conquest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RidsdalePanorma.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/RidsdalePanorma.jpg/250px-RidsdalePanorma.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="117" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/RidsdalePanorma.jpg/375px-RidsdalePanorma.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/RidsdalePanorma.jpg/500px-RidsdalePanorma.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="560" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RidsdalePanorma.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A panorama of 15th-century York by <a href="/wiki/E_Ridsdale_Tate" title="E Ridsdale Tate">E Ridsdale Tate</a>, <a href="/wiki/York_Castle" title="York Castle">York Castle</a> is on the right hand side of the river, opposite the abandoned motte of <a href="/wiki/Baile_Hill,_York" class="mw-redirect" title="Baile Hill, York">Baile Hill</a></div></div></div>
<p>In 1068, two years after the <a href="/wiki/Norman_conquest_of_England" title="Norman conquest of England">Norman conquest of England</a>, the people of York rebelled. Initially they were successful, but upon the arrival of <a href="/wiki/William_I_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="William I of England">William the Conqueror</a> the rebellion was put down. William at once built a wooden fortress on a motte. In 1069, after another rebellion, the king built another timbered castle across the River Ouse. These were destroyed in 1069 and rebuilt by William about the time of his ravaging Northumbria in what is called the "<a href="/wiki/Harrying_of_the_North" title="Harrying of the North">Harrying of the North</a>" where he destroyed everything from York to Durham. The remains of the rebuilt castles, now in stone, are visible on either side of the River Ouse. See Peter Rex's The English Resistance, The Underground War Against the Normans, 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The first stone minster church was badly damaged by fire in the uprising, and the Normans built a minster on a new site. Around the year 1080, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_I_of_York" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomas I of York">Archbishop Thomas</a> started building the cathedral that in time became the current Minster.<sup id="cite_ref-ymhist_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ymhist-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Shambles_shopper_8686.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Shambles_shopper_8686.jpg/220px-Shambles_shopper_8686.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Shambles_shopper_8686.jpg/330px-Shambles_shopper_8686.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Shambles_shopper_8686.jpg/440px-Shambles_shopper_8686.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="1600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Shambles_shopper_8686.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/The_Shambles" title="The Shambles">The Shambles</a> is a medieval shopping street in the city; most of the buildings date from between <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 1350 and 1475</div></div></div>
<p>In the 12th&#160;century York started to prosper. In 1190, <a href="/wiki/York_Castle#12th_century" title="York Castle">York Castle</a> was the site of an infamous <a href="/wiki/12th_century_English_pogroms" class="mw-redirect" title="12th century English pogroms">massacre</a> of its <a href="/wiki/Jew" class="mw-redirect" title="Jew">Jewish</a> inhabitants, in which at least 150 Jews died (although some authorities put the figure as high as 500).<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbcpog_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcpog-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:York_Micklegate_Bar_-_panoramio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/York_Micklegate_Bar_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-York_Micklegate_Bar_-_panoramio.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/York_Micklegate_Bar_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-York_Micklegate_Bar_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/York_Micklegate_Bar_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-York_Micklegate_Bar_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2288" data-file-height="1712" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:York_Micklegate_Bar_-_panoramio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The southern entrance to York, Micklegate Bar. The lower section was built in the 12th century, the top storeys in the 14th. The gates connected to the <a href="/wiki/York_city_walls" title="York city walls">York city walls</a>, some sections of which were built in the 12th to 15th centuries, others in <a href="/wiki/Roman_Britain" title="Roman Britain">Roman</a> times.</div></div></div>
<p>The city, through its location on the River Ouse and its proximity to the <a href="/wiki/Great_North_Road_(Great_Britain)" title="Great North Road (Great Britain)">Great North Road</a>, became a major trading centre. <a href="/wiki/John,_King_of_England" title="John, King of England">King John</a> granted the city's first <a href="/wiki/Charter" title="Charter">charter</a> in 1212,<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> confirming trading rights in England and Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-ymhist_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ymhist-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-coynm_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coynm-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> During the later Middle Ages, York merchants imported wine from France, cloth, wax, canvas, and oats from the <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries" title="Low Countries">Low Countries</a>, timber and furs from the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_region" title="Baltic region">Baltic</a> and exported grain to <a href="/wiki/Gascony" title="Gascony">Gascony</a> and grain and wool to the Low Countries.<sup id="cite_ref-VCH_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VCH-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>York became a major cloth manufacturing and trading centre. <a href="/wiki/Edward_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Edward I">Edward I</a> further stimulated the city's economy by using the city as a base for his war in Scotland. The city was the location of significant unrest during the so-called <a href="/wiki/Peasants%27_Revolt" title="Peasants&#39; Revolt">Peasants' Revolt</a> in 1381. The city acquired an increasing degree of autonomy from central government including the privileges granted by a charter of <a href="/wiki/Richard_II_of_England" title="Richard II of England">Richard II</a> in 1396.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="16th_to_18th_centuries">16th to 18th centuries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 16th to 18th centuries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wall_of_the_ruins,_st_marys_abbey_York_8714.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Wall_of_the_ruins%2C_st_marys_abbey_York_8714.jpg/220px-Wall_of_the_ruins%2C_st_marys_abbey_York_8714.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Wall_of_the_ruins%2C_st_marys_abbey_York_8714.jpg/330px-Wall_of_the_ruins%2C_st_marys_abbey_York_8714.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Wall_of_the_ruins%2C_st_marys_abbey_York_8714.jpg/440px-Wall_of_the_ruins%2C_st_marys_abbey_York_8714.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="1602" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wall_of_the_ruins,_st_marys_abbey_York_8714.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A portion of the ruins of <a href="/wiki/St_Mary%27s_Abbey,_York" title="St Mary&#39;s Abbey, York">St Mary's Abbey, York</a>, founded in 1155, extensively damaged by fire in 1157, rebuilt by 1294 and destroyed during the Dissolution in the 16th century</div></div></div>
<p>The city underwent a period of economic decline during <a href="/wiki/Tudor_period" title="Tudor period">Tudor</a> times. Under <a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII_of_England" title="Henry VIII of England">King Henry VIII</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Monasteries" title="Dissolution of the Monasteries">Dissolution of the Monasteries</a> saw the end of York's many <a href="/wiki/Monastery" title="Monastery">monastic houses</a>, including several orders of <a href="/wiki/Friars" class="mw-redirect" title="Friars">friars</a>, the hospitals of St Nicholas and of St Leonard, the largest such institution in the north of England. This led to the <a href="/wiki/Pilgrimage_of_Grace" title="Pilgrimage of Grace">Pilgrimage of Grace</a>, an uprising of northern Catholics in Yorkshire and Lincolnshire opposed to religious reform. Henry VIII restored his authority by establishing  the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_North" title="Council of the North">Council of the North</a> in York in the dissolved St Mary's Abbey. The city became a trading and service centre during this period.<sup id="cite_ref-coyad_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coyad-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-iadbpm_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iadbpm-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Guy_Fawkes" title="Guy Fawkes">Guy Fawkes</a>, who was born and educated in York, was a member of a group of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> restorationists that planned the <a href="/wiki/Gunpowder_Plot" title="Gunpowder Plot">Gunpowder Plot</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Its aim was to displace <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> rule by blowing up the <a href="/wiki/Houses_of_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Houses of Parliament">Houses of Parliament</a> while King <a href="/wiki/James_I_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="James I of England">James I</a>, the entire Protestant, and even most of the Catholic <a href="/wiki/Aristocracy" title="Aristocracy">aristocracy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nobility" title="Nobility">nobility</a> were inside.
</p><p>In 1644, during the <a href="/wiki/English_Civil_War" title="English Civil War">Civil War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Roundhead" title="Roundhead">Parliamentarians</a> <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_York" title="Siege of York">besieged York</a>, and many medieval houses outside the city walls were lost. The <a href="/wiki/Barbican" title="Barbican">barbican</a> at Walmgate Bar was undermined and explosives laid, but, the plot was discovered. On the arrival of <a href="/wiki/Prince_Rupert_of_the_Rhine" title="Prince Rupert of the Rhine">Prince Rupert</a>, with an army of 15,000&#160;men, the siege was lifted. The Parliamentarians retreated some 6 miles (10&#160;km) from York with Rupert in pursuit, before turning on his army and soundly defeating it at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Marston_Moor" title="Battle of Marston Moor">Battle of Marston Moor</a>. Of Rupert's 15,000&#160;troops, no fewer than 4,000 were killed and 1,500 captured. The siege was renewed; the city could not hold out for much longer, and surrendered to <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Fairfax,_3rd_Lord_Fairfax_of_Cameron" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomas Fairfax, 3rd Lord Fairfax of Cameron">Sir Thomas Fairfax</a><sup id="cite_ref-coyad_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coyad-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> on 15 July.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lower_Petergate_in_York,_England.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Lower_Petergate_in_York%2C_England.jpg/220px-Lower_Petergate_in_York%2C_England.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="326" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Lower_Petergate_in_York%2C_England.jpg/330px-Lower_Petergate_in_York%2C_England.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Lower_Petergate_in_York%2C_England.jpg/440px-Lower_Petergate_in_York%2C_England.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1622" data-file-height="2400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lower_Petergate_in_York,_England.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Low Petergate with the cathedral in the background</div></div></div>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/English_Restoration" class="mw-redirect" title="English Restoration">restoration of the monarchy</a> in 1660, and the removal of the garrison from York in 1688, the city was dominated by the gentry and merchants, although the clergy were still important. Competition from <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingston_upon_Hull" title="Kingston upon Hull">Hull</a>, together with silting of the River Ouse, resulted in York losing its pre-eminent position as a trading centre but the city's role as the social and cultural centre for wealthy northerners was on the rise. York's many elegant <a href="/wiki/Townhouse" title="Townhouse">townhouses</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/Mansion_House,_York" title="Mansion House, York">Lord Mayor's Mansion House</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fairfax_House" title="Fairfax House">Fairfax House</a> date from this period, as do the <a href="/wiki/York_Assembly_Rooms" title="York Assembly Rooms">Assembly Rooms</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Theatre_Royal,_York" class="mw-redirect" title="Theatre Royal, York">Theatre Royal</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/York_Racecourse" title="York Racecourse">racecourse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-iadbpm_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iadbpm-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-coygt_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coygt-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During this general time period, the American city of <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_New_York" title="Province of New York">colony that contained it</a> were renamed after the <a href="/wiki/James_II_of_England" title="James II of England">Duke of York (later King James II)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_history">Modern history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Modern history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:York_City_Walls_-_geograph.org.uk_-_589000.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/York_City_Walls_-_geograph.org.uk_-_589000.jpg/220px-York_City_Walls_-_geograph.org.uk_-_589000.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/York_City_Walls_-_geograph.org.uk_-_589000.jpg/330px-York_City_Walls_-_geograph.org.uk_-_589000.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/York_City_Walls_-_geograph.org.uk_-_589000.jpg/440px-York_City_Walls_-_geograph.org.uk_-_589000.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:York_City_Walls_-_geograph.org.uk_-_589000.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/York_Minster" title="York Minster">Minster</a> as seen from the Station Road <a href="/wiki/York_city_walls" title="York city walls">walls</a></div></div></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047036">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>mak all t'railways cum to York</p><div class="templatequotecite">—&#8201;<cite><a href="/wiki/George_Hudson" title="George Hudson">George Hudson</a><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<p>The railway promoter <a href="/wiki/George_Hudson" title="George Hudson">George Hudson</a> was responsible for bringing the railway to York in 1839. Although Hudson's career as a railway entrepreneur ended in disgrace and bankruptcy, his promotion of York over Leeds, and of his own railway company (the <a href="/wiki/York_and_North_Midland_Railway" title="York and North Midland Railway">York and North Midland Railway</a>), helped establish York as a major railway centre by the late 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:National_Railway_Museum_-_Virgin_91101_(rear).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/National_Railway_Museum_-_Virgin_91101_%28rear%29.JPG/220px-National_Railway_Museum_-_Virgin_91101_%28rear%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/National_Railway_Museum_-_Virgin_91101_%28rear%29.JPG/330px-National_Railway_Museum_-_Virgin_91101_%28rear%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/National_Railway_Museum_-_Virgin_91101_%28rear%29.JPG/440px-National_Railway_Museum_-_Virgin_91101_%28rear%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1366" data-file-height="910" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:National_Railway_Museum_-_Virgin_91101_(rear).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Great hall at the <a href="/wiki/National_Railway_Museum" title="National Railway Museum">National Railway Museum</a></div></div></div>
<p>The introduction of the railways established engineering in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ind1_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ind1-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> At the turn of the 20th&#160;century, the railway accommodated the headquarters and works of the <a href="/wiki/North_Eastern_Railway_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="North Eastern Railway (UK)">North Eastern Railway</a>, which employed more than 5,500 people. The railway was instrumental in the expansion of <a href="/wiki/Rowntree%27s" title="Rowntree&#39;s">Rowntree's Cocoa Works</a>. It was founded in 1862 by Henry Isaac Rowntree, who was joined in 1869 by his brother the philanthropist <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Rowntree_(Philanthropist)" class="mw-redirect" title="Joseph Rowntree (Philanthropist)">Joseph</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-history_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Another chocolate manufacturer, <a href="/wiki/Terry%27s" title="Terry&#39;s">Terry's of York</a>, was a major employer.<sup id="cite_ref-iadbpm_38-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iadbpm-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-coyrapd_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coyrapd-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> By 1900, the railways and confectionery had become the city's two major industries.<sup id="cite_ref-ind1_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ind1-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1942, the city was bombed during the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a> (part of the <a href="/wiki/Baedeker_Blitz" title="Baedeker Blitz">Baedeker Blitz</a>) by the German <a href="/wiki/Luftwaffe" title="Luftwaffe">Luftwaffe</a> and 92 people were killed and hundreds injured.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Buildings damaged in the raid included the <a href="/wiki/York_railway_station" title="York railway station">Railway Station</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rowntree%27s" title="Rowntree&#39;s">Rowntree's</a> Factory, Poppleton Road Primary School, St Martin-le-Grand Church, the <a href="/wiki/Bar_Convent" title="Bar Convent">Bar Convent</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Guildhall,_York" class="mw-redirect" title="Guildhall, York">Guildhall</a> which was left in total disrepair until 1960.
</p><p>With the emergence of tourism, the historic core of York became one of the city's major assets, and in 1968 it was designated a <a href="/wiki/Conservation_area" class="mw-redirect" title="Conservation area">conservation area</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The existing tourist attractions were supplemented by the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/National_Railway_Museum" title="National Railway Museum">National Railway Museum</a> in York in 1975,<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Jorvik_Viking_Centre" title="Jorvik Viking Centre">Jorvik Viking Centre</a> in 1984<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/York_Dungeon" title="York Dungeon">York Dungeon</a> in 1986.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The opening of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_York" title="University of York">University of York</a> in 1963 added to the prosperity of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> In March 2012, <a href="/wiki/York%27s_Chocolate_Story" title="York&#39;s Chocolate Story">York's Chocolate Story</a> opened.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>York was voted European Tourism City of the Year by European Cities Marketing in June 2007, beating 130 other European cities to gain first place, surpassing <a href="/wiki/Gothenburg" title="Gothenburg">Gothenburg</a> in Sweden (second) and <a href="/wiki/Valencia,_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Valencia, Spain">Valencia</a> in Spain (third).<sup id="cite_ref-yorkaward_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yorkaward-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> York was also voted safest place to visit in the 2010 <i><a href="/wiki/Cond%C3%A9_Nast_Traveller" title="Condé Nast Traveller">Condé Nast Traveller</a></i> Readers’ Choice Awards.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> In 2018, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sunday_Times" title="The Sunday Times">The Sunday Times</a></i> deemed York to be its overall 'Best Place to Live' in Britain, highlighting the city's "perfect mix of heritage and hi-tech" and as a "mini-metropolis with cool cafes, destination restaurants, innovative companies – plus the fastest internet in Britain".<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The result was confirmed in a <a href="/wiki/YouGov" title="YouGov">YouGov</a> survey, reported in August 2018, with 92% of respondents saying that they liked the city, more than any of 56 other British cities.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_photography">Early photography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Early photography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>York was a centre of <a href="/wiki/Early_photography" class="mw-redirect" title="Early photography">early photography</a>, as described by Hugh Murray in his 1986 book <i>Photographs and Photographers of York: The Early Years, 1844–79</i>. Photographers who had studios in York included <a href="/wiki/William_Hayes_(photographer)" title="William Hayes (photographer)">William Hayes</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Pumphrey" title="William Pumphrey">William Pumphrey</a>, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Augustus_Mahalski&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Augustus Mahalski (page does not exist)">Augustus Mahalski</a> who operated on Davygate and Low Petergate in the 19th century, having come to England as a refugee after serving as a <a href="/wiki/Uhlan" title="Uhlan">Polish lancer</a> in the Austro-Hungarian war.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_government">Local government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Local government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>For a detailed history of local government in the City of York, see <a href="/wiki/City_of_York_Council" title="City of York Council">City of York Council</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:York_Guildhall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/York_Guildhall.jpg/220px-York_Guildhall.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/York_Guildhall.jpg/330px-York_Guildhall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/York_Guildhall.jpg/440px-York_Guildhall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3704" data-file-height="2658" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:York_Guildhall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Guildhall,_York" class="mw-redirect" title="Guildhall, York">York Guildhall</a> is the seat of local government</div></div></div><p>The City of York is governed by the <a href="/wiki/City_of_York_Council" title="City of York Council">City of York Council</a>. It is a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_authority" title="Unitary authority">unitary authority</a> that operates on a <a href="/wiki/Leader_and_cabinet" class="mw-redirect" title="Leader and cabinet">leader and cabinet</a> style of governance, having the powers of a non-metropolitan county and district council combined. It provides a full range of local government services including Council Tax billing, libraries, social services, processing planning applications, waste collection and disposal, and it is a local education authority. The city council consists of 47 councillors<sup id="cite_ref-councillors_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-councillors-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> representing 21 <a href="/wiki/Ward_(electoral_subdivision)" title="Ward (electoral subdivision)">wards</a>, with two or three per ward serving four-year terms. Its headquarters are at the <a href="/wiki/York_Guildhall" title="York Guildhall">Guildhall</a> and West Offices in the city centre.
</p><p>York is divided into 21 administrative wards: <a href="/wiki/Acomb,_North_Yorkshire" title="Acomb, North Yorkshire">Acomb</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bishopthorpe" title="Bishopthorpe">Bishopthorpe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clifton,_York" title="Clifton, York">Clifton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copmanthorpe" title="Copmanthorpe">Copmanthorpe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dringhouses" title="Dringhouses">Dringhouses</a> and <a href="/wiki/Woodthorpe,_North_Yorkshire" title="Woodthorpe, North Yorkshire">Woodthorpe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fishergate" title="Fishergate">Fishergate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fulford,_North_Yorkshire" title="Fulford, North Yorkshire">Fulford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heslington" title="Heslington">Heslington</a>, Guildhall, <a href="/wiki/Haxby" title="Haxby">Haxby</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wigginton,_North_Yorkshire" title="Wigginton, North Yorkshire">Wigginton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heworth,_York" title="Heworth, York">Heworth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heworth_Without" title="Heworth Without">Heworth Without</a>, <a href="/wiki/Holgate,_North_Yorkshire" title="Holgate, North Yorkshire">Holgate</a>, Hull Road, <a href="/wiki/Huntington,_City_of_York" title="Huntington, City of York">Huntington</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Earswick" title="New Earswick">New Earswick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Micklegate" title="Micklegate">Micklegate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Osbaldwick" title="Osbaldwick">Osbaldwick</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Derwent_(ward)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Derwent (ward) (page does not exist)">Derwent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rawcliffe,_York" title="Rawcliffe, York">Rawcliffe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Clifton_Without" title="Clifton Without">Clifton Without</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rural_West_York" title="Rural West York">Rural West York</a>, <a href="/wiki/Strensall" title="Strensall">Strensall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Westfield,_York" class="mw-redirect" title="Westfield, York">Westfield</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wheldrake" title="Wheldrake">Wheldrake</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The members of the cabinet, led by the <a href="/wiki/Leader_of_the_City_of_York_Council" title="Leader of the City of York Council">Council Leader</a>, makes decisions on their portfolio areas individually.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Following the <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Act_2000" title="Local Government Act 2000">Local Government Act 2000</a>, the Council Leader commands the <a href="/wiki/Confidence_and_supply" title="Confidence and supply">confidence</a> of the city council; the leader of the largest political group and head of the City of York Council. The Leader of the Council and the cabinet (consisting of all the executive councillors) are collectively <a href="/wiki/Accountability" title="Accountability">accountable</a> for their policies and actions to the city council. The current Council Leader, <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a>' Cllr Keith Aspden, was appointed on 22 May 2019, following the <a href="/wiki/2019_City_of_York_Council_election" title="2019 City of York Council election">2019 City of York Council election</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Helen%27s_Square,_York.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/St_Helen%27s_Square%2C_York.jpg/220px-St_Helen%27s_Square%2C_York.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/St_Helen%27s_Square%2C_York.jpg/330px-St_Helen%27s_Square%2C_York.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/St_Helen%27s_Square%2C_York.jpg/440px-St_Helen%27s_Square%2C_York.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4913" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Helen%27s_Square,_York.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Mansion_House,_York" title="Mansion House, York">Mansion House</a> is home to the <a href="/wiki/Lord_Mayor_of_York" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Mayor of York">Lord Mayor of York</a></div></div></div><p>York's first citizen and civic head is the <a href="/wiki/Lord_Mayor_of_York" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Mayor of York">Lord Mayor</a>, who is the <a href="/wiki/Chairman" class="mw-redirect" title="Chairman">chairman</a> of the City of York Council. The appointment is made by the city council each year in May, at the same time appointing the Sheriff, the city's other civic head. The offices of Lord Mayor and Sheriff are purely ceremonial. The Lord Mayor carries out civic and ceremonial duties in addition to chairing full council meetings.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The incumbent Lord Mayor since 22 May 2019 is Councillor <a href="/wiki/Janet_Looker" title="Janet Looker">Janet Looker</a>, and the Sheriff is Jo Trythall.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>York Youth Council consists of several young people who negotiate with the councillors to get better facilities for York's young people, and who also elect York's <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Youth_Parliament" title="Member of Youth Parliament">Member of Youth Parliament</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As a result of the <a href="/wiki/2019_City_of_York_Council_election" title="2019 City of York Council election">2019 City of York Council election</a> the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative Party</a> was reduced to two seats. The <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a> had 21 councillors. The <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour Party</a> had 17 councillors and the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales" title="Green Party of England and Wales">Green Party</a> had four with three Independents.<sup id="cite_ref-bbccoun_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbccoun-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Due to <a href="/wiki/No_overall_control" title="No overall control">no overall control</a>, the Liberal Democrats and the Green Party agreed to form a coalition on 14 May 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<td colspan="24" style="width:4px; background:#fff;">&#160;

<p>York is the traditional <a href="/wiki/County_town" title="County town">county town</a> of <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire" title="Yorkshire">Yorkshire</a>, and therefore did not form part of any of its three historic <a href="/wiki/Riding_(division)" class="mw-redirect" title="Riding (division)">ridings</a>, or divisions. Its Mayor has had the status of Lord Mayor since 1370. York is an ancient <a href="/wiki/Borough" title="Borough">borough</a>, and was reformed by the <a href="/wiki/Municipal_Corporations_Act_1835" title="Municipal Corporations Act 1835">Municipal Corporations Act 1835</a> to form a <a href="/wiki/Municipal_borough" title="Municipal borough">municipal borough</a>. It gained the status of a <a href="/wiki/County_borough" title="County borough">county borough</a> in 1889, under the <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Act_1888" title="Local Government Act 1888">Local Government Act 1888</a>, and existed so until 1974, when, under the <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Act_1972" title="Local Government Act 1972">Local Government Act 1972</a>, it became a <a href="/wiki/Non-metropolitan_district" title="Non-metropolitan district">non-metropolitan district</a> in the county of North Yorkshire, whilst retaining its Lord Mayor, its Sheriff and Aldermen.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> As a result of <a href="/wiki/1990s_UK_local_government_reform" class="mw-redirect" title="1990s UK local government reform">1990s UK local government reform</a>, York regained unitary status and saw a substantial alteration in its borders, taking in parts of <a href="/wiki/Selby_(district)" class="mw-redirect" title="Selby (district)">Selby</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harrogate_(borough)" class="mw-redirect" title="Harrogate (borough)">Harrogate</a> districts, and about half the population of the <a href="/wiki/Ryedale" title="Ryedale">Ryedale</a> district.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The new boundary was imposed after central government rejected the former city council's own proposal.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parliamentary_constituencies">Parliamentary constituencies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Parliamentary constituencies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
