<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_services">Public services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Public services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:York_Central_Library_-_geograph.org.uk_-_765971.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/York_Central_Library_-_geograph.org.uk_-_765971.jpg/220px-York_Central_Library_-_geograph.org.uk_-_765971.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/York_Central_Library_-_geograph.org.uk_-_765971.jpg/330px-York_Central_Library_-_geograph.org.uk_-_765971.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/York_Central_Library_-_geograph.org.uk_-_765971.jpg/440px-York_Central_Library_-_geograph.org.uk_-_765971.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="406" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:York_Central_Library_-_geograph.org.uk_-_765971.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>York's Central Library is located in the city centre</div></div></div>
<p>Under the requirements of the <a href="/wiki/Municipal_Corporations_Act_1835" title="Municipal Corporations Act 1835">Municipal Corporations Act 1835</a>, York City Council appointed a <a href="/wiki/Watch_committee" title="Watch committee">watch committee</a> which established a police force and appointed a chief constable.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> On 1 June 1968 the York City, East Riding of Yorkshire and North Riding of Yorkshire police forces were amalgamated to form the <a href="/wiki/York_and_North_East_Yorkshire_Police" title="York and North East Yorkshire Police">York and North East Yorkshire Police</a>. Since 1974, <a href="/wiki/Home_Office" title="Home Office">Home Office</a> policing in York has been provided by the <a href="/wiki/North_Yorkshire_Police" title="North Yorkshire Police">North Yorkshire Police</a>. The force's central headquarters for policing York and nearby <a href="/wiki/Selby_(district)" class="mw-redirect" title="Selby (district)">Selby</a> are in Fulford.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
<a href="/wiki/Fire_service_in_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Fire service in the United Kingdom">Statutory emergency fire and rescue service</a> is provided by the <a href="/wiki/North_Yorkshire_Fire_and_Rescue_Service" title="North Yorkshire Fire and Rescue Service">North Yorkshire Fire and Rescue Service</a>, whose headquarters is at <a href="/wiki/Northallerton" title="Northallerton">Northallerton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:York_Hospital_Front_entrance.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/York_Hospital_Front_entrance.jpg/220px-York_Hospital_Front_entrance.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/York_Hospital_Front_entrance.jpg/330px-York_Hospital_Front_entrance.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/York_Hospital_Front_entrance.jpg/440px-York_Hospital_Front_entrance.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="676" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:York_Hospital_Front_entrance.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>York Hospital is the city's primary medical facility.</div></div></div>
<p>The city's first hospital, York County Hospital, opened in 1740 in Monkgate<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> funded by public subscription. It closed in 1976 when it was replaced by <a href="/wiki/York_Hospital" title="York Hospital">York Hospital</a>, which opened the same year and gained <a href="/wiki/NHS_foundation_trust" title="NHS foundation trust">Foundation status</a> in April 2007. It has 524 adult inpatient beds and 127 special purpose beds providing general healthcare and some specialist inpatient, daycase and outpatient services.<sup id="cite_ref-YDH_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YDH-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> It is also known as York District Hospital and YDH.<sup id="cite_ref-YDH_136-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YDH-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Ambulance_Service" title="Yorkshire Ambulance Service">Yorkshire Ambulance Service</a> NHS Trust was formed on 1 July 2006 bringing together South Yorkshire Ambulance Service, West Yorkshire Metropolitan Ambulance Service and the North and East Yorkshire parts of Tees, East and North Yorkshire Ambulance Service to provide patient transport.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Other forms of health care are provided for locally by clinics and surgeries.
</p><p>The city's first subscription library opened in 1794.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> The first free <a href="/wiki/Public_library" title="Public library">public library</a>, the <a href="/wiki/York_Library" title="York Library">York Library</a>, was built on Clifford Street in 1893, to mark <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a>'s jubilee. A new building was erected on Museum Street in 1927, and this is still the library today; it was extended in 1934 and 1938.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 1998 <a href="/wiki/Waste_management" title="Waste management">waste management</a> has been co-ordinated via the York and North Yorkshire Waste Partnership.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> York's <a href="/wiki/Distribution_Network_Operator" class="mw-redirect" title="Distribution Network Operator">Distribution Network Operator</a> for electricity is <a href="/wiki/CE_Electric_UK" class="mw-redirect" title="CE Electric UK">CE Electric UK</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> there are no <a href="/wiki/Power_station" title="Power station">power stations</a> in the city. <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Water" title="Yorkshire Water">Yorkshire Water</a>, which has a local water extraction plant on the <a href="/wiki/River_Derwent,_Yorkshire" title="River Derwent, Yorkshire">River Derwent</a> at Elvington, manages York's <a href="/wiki/Drinking_water" title="Drinking water">drinking</a> and <a href="/wiki/Waste_water" class="mw-redirect" title="Waste water">waste water</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:York_Crown_Court.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/York_Crown_Court.jpg/220px-York_Crown_Court.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/York_Crown_Court.jpg/330px-York_Crown_Court.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/York_Crown_Court.jpg/440px-York_Crown_Court.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1632" data-file-height="1232" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:York_Crown_Court.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>York Crown Court</div></div></div>
<p>The city has a <a href="/wiki/Magistrates%27_court_(England_and_Wales)" title="Magistrates&#39; court (England and Wales)">magistrates' court</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> and venues for the <a href="/wiki/Crown_Court" title="Crown Court">Crown Court</a><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/County_Court_(England_and_Wales)" title="County Court (England and Wales)">County Court</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
The Crown Court House was designed by the architect <a href="/wiki/John_Carr_(architect)" title="John Carr (architect)">John Carr</a>, next to the then prison (including execution area).<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Between 1773 and 1777, the Grand Jury House was replaced by John Carr's elegant Court House for the <a href="/wiki/Assizes" title="Assizes">Assizes</a> of the whole county. The Female Prison was built opposite and mirrors the court building positioned around a circular lawn which became known as the "Eye of the Ridings", or the "Eye of York".
</p><p>1776 saw the last recorded instance of a wife hanged and burnt for poisoning her husband. <a href="/wiki/Horse_theft" title="Horse theft">Horse theft</a> was a <a href="/wiki/Capital_offence" class="mw-redirect" title="Capital offence">capital offence</a>. The culprits of lesser crimes were brought to court by the city constables and would face a fine. The corporation employed a "common informer" whose task was to bring criminals to justice.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The former prison is now the <a href="/wiki/York_Castle_Museum" title="York Castle Museum">Castle Museum</a> but still contains the cells.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>York's location on the River Ouse and in the centre of the Vale of York means that it has always had a significant position in the nation's transport system.<sup id="cite_ref-VCH_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VCH-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The city grew up as a river port at the confluence of the <a href="/wiki/River_Ouse,_Yorkshire" title="River Ouse, Yorkshire">River Ouse</a> and the <a href="/wiki/River_Foss" title="River Foss">River Foss</a>. The Ouse was originally a <a href="/wiki/Tidal_river" title="Tidal river">tidal river</a>, accessible to seagoing ships of the time. Today both of these rivers remain navigable, although the Foss is only navigable for a short distance above the confluence. A <a href="/wiki/Canal_lock" class="mw-redirect" title="Canal lock">lock</a> at <a href="/wiki/Naburn" title="Naburn">Naburn</a> on the Ouse to the south of York means that the river in York is no longer tidal.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Until the end of the 20th&#160;century, the Ouse was used by <a href="/wiki/Barge" title="Barge">barges</a> to carry freight between York and the port of <a href="/wiki/Kingston_upon_Hull" title="Kingston upon Hull">Hull</a>. The last significant such traffic was the supply of <a href="/wiki/Newsprint" title="Newsprint">newsprint</a> to the local newspaper's Foss-side print works, which continued until 1997. Today navigation is almost exclusively leisure-oriented.
</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin:0 auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:1008px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a href="/wiki/File:York_night.JPG" class="image" title="Panorama of the River Ouse looking south from Lendal Bridge"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/York_night.JPG/1000px-York_night.JPG" decoding="async" width="1000" height="145" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/York_night.JPG/1500px-York_night.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/York_night.JPG/2000px-York_night.JPG 2x" data-file-width="8046" data-file-height="1169" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:York_night.JPG" title="File:York night.JPG"> </a></div>Panorama of the <a href="/wiki/River_Ouse,_Yorkshire" title="River Ouse, Yorkshire">River Ouse</a> looking south from Lendal Bridge</div></div></div>
<p>Like most cities founded by the Romans, York is well served by long-distance trunk roads. The city lies at the intersection of the <a href="/wiki/A19_road" title="A19 road">A19 road</a> from <a href="/wiki/Doncaster" title="Doncaster">Doncaster</a> to <a href="/wiki/Tyneside" title="Tyneside">Tyneside</a>, the <a href="/wiki/A59_road" title="A59 road">A59 road</a> from <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a> to York, the <a href="/wiki/A64_road" title="A64 road">A64 road</a> from <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a> to <a href="/wiki/Scarborough,_North_Yorkshire" title="Scarborough, North Yorkshire">Scarborough</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/A1079_road" title="A1079 road">A1079 road</a> from York to <a href="/wiki/Kingston_upon_Hull" title="Kingston upon Hull">Hull</a>. The A64 road provides the principal link to the motorway network, linking York to both the <a href="/wiki/A1_road_(Great_Britain)" title="A1 road (Great Britain)">A1(M)</a> and the <a href="/wiki/M1_motorway" title="M1 motorway">M1 motorways</a> at a distance of about 10 miles (15&#160;km) from the city. The transpennine <a href="/wiki/M62_motorway" title="M62 motorway">M62 motorway</a> is less than 20 miles (30&#160;km) away providing links to <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a> and Liverpool.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stonegate_in_York_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1261035.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Stonegate_in_York_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1261035.jpg/220px-Stonegate_in_York_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1261035.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Stonegate_in_York_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1261035.jpg/330px-Stonegate_in_York_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1261035.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Stonegate_in_York_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1261035.jpg/440px-Stonegate_in_York_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1261035.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="427" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stonegate_in_York_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1261035.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Stonegate is pedestrianised during the day</div></div></div>
<p>The city is surrounded on all sides by an outer ring road, at a distance of some 3 miles (5&#160;km) from the centre of the city, which allows through traffic to by-pass the city. The street plan of the historic core of the city dates from medieval times and is not suitable for modern traffic. As a consequence many of the routes inside the city walls are designated as <a href="/wiki/Car-free_zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Car-free zone">car free</a> during business hours or restrict traffic entirely. To alleviate this situation, six bus based <a href="/wiki/York_Park_and_Ride" class="mw-redirect" title="York Park and Ride">park and ride</a> sites operate in York. The sites are located towards the edge of the urban area, with easy access from the ring road, and allow out of town visitors to complete their journey into the city centre by bus.<sup id="cite_ref-coypar_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coypar-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:York_station_rush_hour.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/York_station_rush_hour.jpg/220px-York_station_rush_hour.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/York_station_rush_hour.jpg/330px-York_station_rush_hour.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/York_station_rush_hour.jpg/440px-York_station_rush_hour.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1268" data-file-height="840" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:York_station_rush_hour.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/York_railway_station" title="York railway station">York railway station</a></div></div></div>
<p>York has been a major railway centre since the first line arrived in 1839 at the beginning of the railway age. For many years the city hosted the headquarters and works of the <a href="/wiki/North_Eastern_Railway_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="North Eastern Railway (UK)">North Eastern Railway</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-coyrapd_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coyrapd-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/York_railway_station" title="York railway station">York railway station</a> is a principal stop on the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_Main_Line" title="East Coast Main Line">East Coast Main Line</a> from London to <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="Newcastle upon Tyne">Newcastle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>. It takes less than two hours to get to York from London by rail, with at least 25 direct trains each weekday. The station is also served by long distance trains on <a href="/wiki/CrossCountry" title="CrossCountry">CrossCountry</a> services linking Edinburgh and Newcastle with destinations in south and west England via <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-coyrail_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coyrail-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/TransPennine_Express" title="TransPennine Express">TransPennine Express</a> provide a frequent service of semi-fast trains linking York to Newcastle, <a href="/wiki/Scarborough,_North_Yorkshire" title="Scarborough, North Yorkshire">Scarborough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a>, Manchester, <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">Manchester Airport</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a>. Local stopping services by <a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern</a> connect York to Selby, <a href="/wiki/Harrogate" title="Harrogate">Harrogate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingston_upon_Hull" title="Kingston upon Hull">Hull</a>, Leeds, <a href="/wiki/Sheffield" title="Sheffield">Sheffield</a> and many intermediate points, as well as many other stations across Greater Manchester and Lancashire.<sup id="cite_ref-coyrail_150-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coyrail-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>York has an airfield at the former <a href="/wiki/RAF_Elvington" title="RAF Elvington">RAF Elvington</a>, some 7 miles (11&#160;km) south-east of the city centre, which is the home of the <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Air_Museum" title="Yorkshire Air Museum">Yorkshire Air Museum</a>. Elvington is used for <a href="/wiki/Private_aviation" title="Private aviation">private aviation</a>. In 2003 plans were drafted to expand the site for business aviation or a full commercial service.<sup id="cite_ref-tpelb_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tpelb-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ftr_bus_in_Station_Road,_York_railway_station,_19002_(YK06_ATV),_5_October_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Ftr_bus_in_Station_Road%2C_York_railway_station%2C_19002_%28YK06_ATV%29%2C_5_October_2008.jpg/220px-Ftr_bus_in_Station_Road%2C_York_railway_station%2C_19002_%28YK06_ATV%29%2C_5_October_2008.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Ftr_bus_in_Station_Road%2C_York_railway_station%2C_19002_%28YK06_ATV%29%2C_5_October_2008.jpg/330px-Ftr_bus_in_Station_Road%2C_York_railway_station%2C_19002_%28YK06_ATV%29%2C_5_October_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Ftr_bus_in_Station_Road%2C_York_railway_station%2C_19002_%28YK06_ATV%29%2C_5_October_2008.jpg/440px-Ftr_bus_in_Station_Road%2C_York_railway_station%2C_19002_%28YK06_ATV%29%2C_5_October_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1944" data-file-height="1296" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ftr_bus_in_Station_Road,_York_railway_station,_19002_(YK06_ATV),_5_October_2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A York <a href="/wiki/FTR_(bus)" title="FTR (bus)">FTR bus</a></div></div></div>
<p>York is linked to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">Manchester Airport</a> by an hourly direct <a href="/wiki/TransPennine_Express" title="TransPennine Express">TransPennine Express</a> train, giving access to the principal airport serving the north of England, with connections to many destinations in Europe, North America, Africa, and Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-coyrail_150-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coyrail-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Bradford_Airport" title="Leeds Bradford Airport">Leeds Bradford Airport</a> is closer to York but the hourly <i>York Air Coach</i> service operated by <a href="/wiki/First_York" title="First York">First York</a> was withdrawn as of April 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-fgyac_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fgyac-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> Leeds Bradford Airport provides connections to most major European and North African airports as well as <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>.
</p><p>Public transport within the city is largely bus-based. <a href="/wiki/First_York" title="First York">First York</a> operates the majority of the city's local bus services, as well as the <a href="/wiki/York_park_and_ride" title="York park and ride">York park and ride</a> services. York was the location of the first implementation of FirstGroup's experimental and controversial <a href="/wiki/FTR_(bus)" title="FTR (bus)">FTR bus concept</a>, which sought to confer the advantages of a modern tramway system at a lower cost.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> The service was withdrawn following an election manifesto pledge by the Labour Group at the 2011 local government election.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Transdev_York" class="mw-redirect" title="Transdev York">Transdev York</a> also operates a large number of local bus services. Open-top tourist and sightseeing buses are operated by Transdev York on behalf of <a href="/wiki/City_Sightseeing" title="City Sightseeing">City Sightseeing</a>.
</p><p>Rural services, linking local towns and villages with York, are provided by a number of companies with Transdev York, EYMS, and Reliance operating most of them.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>
Longer-distance bus services are provided by a number of operators, including <a href="/wiki/Arriva_Yorkshire" title="Arriva Yorkshire">Arriva Yorkshire</a> services to Selby, <a href="/wiki/East_Yorkshire_Motor_Services" class="mw-redirect" title="East Yorkshire Motor Services">East Yorkshire Motor Services</a> routes to Hull, Beverley, Driffield, Market Weighton and Pocklington, and <a href="/wiki/Harrogate_Bus_Company" title="Harrogate Bus Company">Harrogate Bus Company</a> services to <a href="/wiki/Knaresborough" title="Knaresborough">Knaresborough</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harrogate" title="Harrogate">Harrogate</a>. <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Coastliner" class="mw-redirect" title="Yorkshire Coastliner">Yorkshire Coastliner</a> links <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a> via York with Scarborough, <a href="/wiki/Filey" title="Filey">Filey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bridlington" title="Bridlington">Bridlington</a> and <a href="/wiki/Whitby" title="Whitby">Whitby</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_Transport_Plan_2006">Local Transport Plan 2006</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Local Transport Plan 2006">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>English local authorities are required to produce Local Transport Plans (LTPs), strategies for developing local integrated transport as part of a longer-term vision. LTPs are used by central government to allocate funding for transport schemes. The final Local Transport Plan 2006–2011 for York was submitted to central government in March 2006. The plan addresses the fact that traffic in York is predicted to grow considerably over the coming years. The key aims of the plan are to ease congestion and improve accessibility, air quality and safety. Major funding allocations earmarked for the first five years of the plan's life span include outer ring road improvements, improved management of the highway network, improvements to the bus network including park and ride services, provision of off-road walking and cycling routes, air quality improvements and safety measures.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_York" title="List of schools in York">List of schools in York</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bootham_School_-_geograph.org.uk_-_673245.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Bootham_School_-_geograph.org.uk_-_673245.jpg/220px-Bootham_School_-_geograph.org.uk_-_673245.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Bootham_School_-_geograph.org.uk_-_673245.jpg/330px-Bootham_School_-_geograph.org.uk_-_673245.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Bootham_School_-_geograph.org.uk_-_673245.jpg/440px-Bootham_School_-_geograph.org.uk_-_673245.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bootham_School_-_geograph.org.uk_-_673245.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bootham School was established by Quakers in 1823</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_York" title="University of York">University of York</a>'s main campus is on the southern edge of the city at <a href="/wiki/Heslington" title="Heslington">Heslington</a>.   The Department of Archaeology and the graduate Centres for Eighteenth Century Studies and Medieval Studies are located in the historic King's Manor in the city centre.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> It was York's only institution with university status until 2006, when the more centrally located <a href="/wiki/York_St_John_University" title="York St John University">York St John University</a>, formerly an autonomous college of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Leeds" title="University of Leeds">University of Leeds</a>, attained full university status. The city formerly hosted a branch of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Law" title="University of Law">University of Law</a> before it moved to Leeds. The University of York also has a  medical school, <a href="/wiki/Hull_York_Medical_School" title="Hull York Medical School">Hull York Medical School</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The city has two major further education institutions. <a href="/wiki/York_College_(York)" title="York College (York)">York College</a> is an amalgamation of York Technical College and York Sixth Form College. Students there study a very wide range of academic and vocational courses, and range from <a href="/wiki/School_leaving_age" class="mw-redirect" title="School leaving age">school leavers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sixth_form" title="Sixth form">sixth formers</a> to people training to make career moves.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Askham_Bryan_College" title="Askham Bryan College">Askham Bryan College</a> offers further education courses, foundation and honours degrees, specialising in more vocational subjects such as horticulture, agriculture, animal management and even <a href="/wiki/Golf_course" title="Golf course">golf course</a> management.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:York_central_hall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/York_central_hall.jpg/220px-York_central_hall.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/York_central_hall.jpg/330px-York_central_hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/York_central_hall.jpg/440px-York_central_hall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2173" data-file-height="1449" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:York_central_hall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/University_of_York" title="University of York">University of York</a>, view across the lake to Central Hall</div></div></div>
<p>There are 70 <a href="/wiki/Local_Education_Authority" class="mw-redirect" title="Local Education Authority">local council</a> schools with over 24,000 pupils in the City of York Council area.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> The City of York Council manages most primary and secondary schools within the city. Primary schools cover education from ages 5–11, with some offering early years education from age 3. From 11–16 education is provided by 10 secondary schools, four of which offer additional education up to the age of 18.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> In 2007 Oaklands Sports College and Lowfield Comprehensive School merged to become one school known as <a href="/wiki/York_High_School,_York" title="York High School, York">York High School</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>York also has several private schools. <a href="/wiki/St_Peter%27s_School,_York" title="St Peter&#39;s School, York">St Peter's School</a> was founded in 627. The scholar <a href="/wiki/Alcuin" title="Alcuin">Alcuin</a>, who went on to serve <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a>, taught there.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> It was also the school attended by <a href="/wiki/Guy_Fawkes" title="Guy Fawkes">Guy Fawkes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> Two schools have <a href="/wiki/Quaker" class="mw-redirect" title="Quaker">Quaker</a> origins: <a href="/wiki/Bootham_School" title="Bootham School">Bootham School</a> is <a href="/wiki/Co-education" class="mw-redirect" title="Co-education">co-educational</a><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/The_Mount_School,_York" title="The Mount School, York">The Mount School</a> is all-girls.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> On the outskirts of the city is <a href="/wiki/Queen_Margaret%27s_School,_York" title="Queen Margaret&#39;s School, York">Queen Margaret's School</a>. Pupils from <a href="/wiki/The_Minster_School,_York" title="The Minster School, York">The Minster School, York</a> sing in York Minster choir.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatre">Theatre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Theatre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Theatre_Royal_3.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Theatre_Royal_3.JPG/220px-Theatre_Royal_3.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Theatre_Royal_3.JPG/330px-Theatre_Royal_3.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Theatre_Royal_3.JPG/440px-Theatre_Royal_3.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1296" data-file-height="972" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Theatre_Royal_3.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Theatre_Royal,_York" class="mw-redirect" title="Theatre Royal, York">Theatre Royal</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/York_Theatre_Royal" title="York Theatre Royal">Theatre Royal</a>, which was established in 1744, produces an annual pantomime which attracts loyal audiences from around the country to see its veteran star, <a href="/wiki/Berwick_Kaler" title="Berwick Kaler">Berwick Kaler</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Grand_Opera_House,_York" title="Grand Opera House, York">Grand Opera House</a> and Joseph Rowntree Theatre also offer a variety of productions.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> The city is home to the <a href="/wiki/Riding_Lights_Theatre_Company" title="Riding Lights Theatre Company">Riding Lights Theatre Company</a>, which as well as operating a busy national touring department, also operates a busy youth theatre and educational departments. York is also home to a number of amateur dramatic groups.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> The Department of Theatre, Film and Television and Student Societies of the University of York put on public drama performances.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:York_Opera.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/York_Opera.jpg/220px-York_Opera.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/York_Opera.jpg/330px-York_Opera.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/York_Opera.jpg/440px-York_Opera.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:York_Opera.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Interior of York's Grand Opera House</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/York_Mystery_Plays" title="York Mystery Plays">York Mystery Plays</a> are performed in public at intervals, using texts based on the original medieval plays of this type that were performed by the guilds – often with specific connections to the subject matter of each play. (For instance the Shipwrights' Play is the <i>Building of Noah's Ark</i> and the fish-sellers and mariners the <i>Landing of Noah's Ark</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> The York Cycle of Mystery Plays or Pageants is the most complete in England. Originally performed from wagons at various locations around the city from the 14th century until 1570, they were revived in 1951 during the <a href="/wiki/Festival_of_Britain" title="Festival of Britain">Festival of Britain</a>, when York was one of the cities with a regional festival.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> They became part of the York City Festival every three years and later four years. They were mostly produced in a temporary open-air theatre within the ruins of St. Mary's Abbey, using some professional but mostly amateur actors. Lead actors have included <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Timothy" title="Christopher Timothy">Christopher Timothy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robson_Green" title="Robson Green">Robson Green</a> (in the role of Christ) and Dame <a href="/wiki/Judi_Dench" title="Judi Dench">Judi Dench</a> as a school girl, in 1951, 1954 and 1957. (She remains a Patron of the plays). The cycle was presented in the Theatre Royal in 1992 and 1996, within York Minster in 2000 and in 2002, 2006 and 2010 by Guild groups from wagons in the squares, in the Dean's Park, or at the Eye of York.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> They go around the streets, recreating the original productions. In 2012, the York Mystery Plays were performed between 2 and 27 August at <a href="/wiki/St_Mary%27s_Abbey,_York" title="St Mary&#39;s Abbey, York">St. Mary's Abbey</a> in the <a href="/wiki/York_Museum_Gardens" title="York Museum Gardens">York Museum Gardens</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_St_Olave%27s" title="Academy of St Olave&#39;s">Academy of St Olave's</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Chamber_orchestra" class="mw-redirect" title="Chamber orchestra">chamber orchestra</a> which gives concerts in <a href="/wiki/St_Olave%27s_Church,_York" title="St Olave&#39;s Church, York">St Olave's Church, Marygate</a>, is one of the music groups that perform regularly in York.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> A former church, <a href="/wiki/Medieval_churches_of_York#St_Margaret,_Walmgate" class="mw-redirect" title="Medieval churches of York">St Margaret's, Walmgate</a>, is the <a href="/wiki/National_Centre_for_Early_Music" title="National Centre for Early Music">National Centre for Early Music</a>, which hosts concerts, broadcasts, competitions and events including the <a href="/wiki/York_Early_Music_Festival" title="York Early Music Festival">York Early Music Festival</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> Students, staff and visiting artists of <a href="/wiki/York_St_John_University" title="York St John University">York St John University</a> music department regularly perform lunchtime concerts in the University chapel. The staff and students of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_York" title="University of York">University of York</a> also perform in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="York_ham">York ham</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: York ham">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:York_ham.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/York_ham.jpg/220px-York_ham.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="197" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/York_ham.jpg/330px-York_ham.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/York_ham.jpg/440px-York_ham.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1854" data-file-height="1658" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:York_ham.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>York Ham</div></div></div>
<p>One of the notable local products is York ham,<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> a mild-flavoured <a href="/wiki/Ham" title="Ham">ham</a> with delicate pink colouring. It is traditionally served with <a href="/wiki/Madeira_wine#Characteristics" title="Madeira wine">Madeira Sauce</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> As a lightly smoked, dry-cured ham, York ham is saltier but milder in flavour than other European dry-cured hams.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> Folklore has it that the oak construction for York Minster provided the sawdust for smoking the ham. Robert Burrow Atkinson's butchery shop, in Blossom Street, is the birthplace of the original "York Ham" and the reason why the premises became famous.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gastronomy">Gastronomy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Gastronomy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Betty%27s_Cafe_Tea_Rooms,_York_(geograph_407877).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Betty%27s_Cafe_Tea_Rooms%2C_York_%28geograph_407877%29.jpg/220px-Betty%27s_Cafe_Tea_Rooms%2C_York_%28geograph_407877%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Betty%27s_Cafe_Tea_Rooms%2C_York_%28geograph_407877%29.jpg/330px-Betty%27s_Cafe_Tea_Rooms%2C_York_%28geograph_407877%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Betty%27s_Cafe_Tea_Rooms%2C_York_%28geograph_407877%29.jpg/440px-Betty%27s_Cafe_Tea_Rooms%2C_York_%28geograph_407877%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Betty%27s_Cafe_Tea_Rooms,_York_(geograph_407877).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bettys_and_Taylors_of_Harrogate" title="Bettys and Taylors of Harrogate">Bettys Café</a> Tea Rooms</div></div></div>
<p>Each September since 1997, York has held an annual Festival of Food and Drink. The aim of the festival is to spotlight food culture in York and North Yorkshire by promoting local food production. The Festival attracts up to 150,000 visitors over 10 days, from all over the country.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the centre of York, in St Helen's Square, there is the York branch of <a href="/wiki/Bettys_and_Taylors_of_Harrogate" title="Bettys and Taylors of Harrogate">Bettys Café</a> Tea Rooms. Bettys' founder, Frederick Belmont, travelled on the maiden voyage of the <i><a href="/wiki/RMS_Queen_Mary" title="RMS Queen Mary">Queen Mary</a></i> in 1936. He was so impressed by the splendour of the ship that he employed the Queen Mary's designers and craftsmen to turn a dilapidated furniture store in York into an elegant café in St Helen's Square. A few years after Bettys opened in York war broke out, and the basement 'Bettys Bar' became a favourite haunt of the thousands of airmen stationed around York. 'Bettys Mirror', on which many of them engraved their signatures with a diamond pen, remains on display today as a tribute to them.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Beer_and_pubs">Beer and pubs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Beer and pubs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kings_Arms_York_-_geograph.org.uk_-_583995.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Kings_Arms_York_-_geograph.org.uk_-_583995.jpg/220px-Kings_Arms_York_-_geograph.org.uk_-_583995.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Kings_Arms_York_-_geograph.org.uk_-_583995.jpg/330px-Kings_Arms_York_-_geograph.org.uk_-_583995.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Kings_Arms_York_-_geograph.org.uk_-_583995.jpg/440px-Kings_Arms_York_-_geograph.org.uk_-_583995.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="425" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kings_Arms_York_-_geograph.org.uk_-_583995.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Kings Arms</div></div></div>
<p>The Assize of Ale is an annual event in the city where people in medieval costume take part in a <a href="/wiki/Pub_crawl" title="Pub crawl">pub crawl</a> to raise money for local charities. It has its origins in the 13th century, when an <a href="/wiki/Assize_of_Bread_and_Ale" title="Assize of Bread and Ale">Assize of Bread and Ale</a> was used to regulate the quality of goods. The current version was resurrected in the 1990s by the Sheriff of York and is led by the Guild of Scriveners.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>  In June 2015 York <a href="/wiki/Campaign_for_Real_Ale" title="Campaign for Real Ale">CAMRA</a> listed 101 pubs on its map of the city centre, some of which are hundreds of years old.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> These include the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Fleece_Inn,_York" title="Golden Fleece Inn, York">Golden Fleece</a>, Ye Olde Starre Inne, noted for its sign which has spanned the street since 1733,<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>  and The Kings Arms, often photographed during floods.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> On 18 June 2016, York CAMRA undertook a "Beer Census" and found 328 unique real ales being served in over 200 pubs in York, reinforcing the city's reputation as a top UK beer destination.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Knavesmire, home of York Racecourse, plays host to Yorkshire's largest beer festival every September run by York CAMRA – York Beer &amp; Cider Festival.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> It is housed in a marquee opposite the grandstand of the racecourse in the enclosure and in 2016 offered over 450 real ales and over 100 ciders.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="UNESCO_status_bids">UNESCO status bids</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: UNESCO status bids">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2010 York's city council and a number of heritage organisations submitted a bid for York's entire city centre to become a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_WHS_1_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_WHS_1-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> This nomination, to the UK's <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Culture,_Media_and_Sport" class="mw-redirect" title="Department for Culture, Media and Sport">Department for Culture, Media and Sport</a> would have included York on a <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_of_the_United_Kingdom#Tentative_list" class="mw-redirect" title="List of World Heritage Sites of the United Kingdom">list of tentative sites</a> to be reviewed by UNESCO itself. York's bid failed, leading to 'disappointment' from the team involved.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_WHS_2_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_WHS_2-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> This indirectly led to the city making a successful bid to be part of the UNESCO <a href="/wiki/Creative_Cities_Network" title="Creative Cities Network">Creative Cities Network</a> as a city of <i>Media Arts</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-YorksPost_MediaCity_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YorksPost_MediaCity-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> It is the fourth of these cities, following <a href="/wiki/Lyon" title="Lyon">Lyon</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>; <a href="/wiki/Enghien-les-Bains" title="Enghien-les-Bains">Enghien-les-Bains</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Sapporo" title="Sapporo">Sapporo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The York area is served by a local newspaper, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Press_(York)" title="The Press (York)">The Press</a></i> (known as the <i>Evening Press</i> until April 2006), <i>The York Advertiser</i> newspaper (based at <i>The Press</i> on Walmgate), and three local radio stations <a href="/wiki/Minster_FM" title="Minster FM">Minster FM</a>, Vale Radio and <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_York" title="BBC Radio York">BBC Radio York</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> Local arts, culture news and events are covered by One&amp;Other.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> Another digital news website is YorkMix run by former print journalists, that incorporates Local News; What's On; Food &amp; Drink; Things To Do and Business sections with articles written by residents and local journalists.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> In August 2016 YorkMix was nominated in two categories in the O2 Media Awards for Yorkshire and The Humber.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 27 November 2013, Ofcom awarded the 12-year local TV licence for the York area to a consortium entitled The York Channel, with the channel due to be on air in spring 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/York_St_John_University" title="York St John University">York St John University</a> has a Film and Television Production department with links to many major industrial partners. The department hosts an annual festival of student work and a showcase of other regional films.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_York" title="University of York">University of York</a> has its own television station <a href="/wiki/York_Student_Television" title="York Student Television">York Student Television</a> (YSTV) and two campus newspapers <i><a href="/wiki/Nouse" title="Nouse">Nouse</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/York_Vision" title="York Vision">York Vision</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> Its radio station <a href="/wiki/University_Radio_York" title="University Radio York">URY</a> is the longest running legal independent radio station in the UK, and was voted <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_1" title="BBC Radio 1">BBC Radio 1</a> Student Radio Station of the Year 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bootham_Crescent_David_Longhurst_Stand_21-03-2009_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Bootham_Crescent_David_Longhurst_Stand_21-03-2009_1.jpg/220px-Bootham_Crescent_David_Longhurst_Stand_21-03-2009_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="109" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Bootham_Crescent_David_Longhurst_Stand_21-03-2009_1.jpg/330px-Bootham_Crescent_David_Longhurst_Stand_21-03-2009_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Bootham_Crescent_David_Longhurst_Stand_21-03-2009_1.jpg/440px-Bootham_Crescent_David_Longhurst_Stand_21-03-2009_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="1410" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bootham_Crescent_David_Longhurst_Stand_21-03-2009_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bootham_Crescent" title="Bootham Crescent">Bootham Crescent</a> is the home ground of <a href="/wiki/York_City_F.C." title="York City F.C.">York City</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:York_City_open_top_bus_2012_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/York_City_open_top_bus_2012_01.jpg/220px-York_City_open_top_bus_2012_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/York_City_open_top_bus_2012_01.jpg/330px-York_City_open_top_bus_2012_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/York_City_open_top_bus_2012_01.jpg/440px-York_City_open_top_bus_2012_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:York_City_open_top_bus_2012_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Celebrations following York’s victory in the <a href="/wiki/2012_Conference_Premier_play-off_Final" title="2012 Conference Premier play-off Final">2012 Play-off final</a></div></div></div>
<p>The city's <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> team is <a href="/wiki/York_City_F.C." title="York City F.C.">York City</a> who are competing in <a href="/wiki/National_League_North" title="National League North">National League North</a> as of the <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_National_League" title="2017–18 National League">2017–18 season</a>. York have played as high as the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Second_Division" title="Football League Second Division">old Second Division</a> but are best known for their 'giant killing' status in cup competitions, having reached the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> semi-final in <a href="/wiki/1954%E2%80%9355_FA_Cup" title="1954–55 FA Cup">1955</a> and beaten <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> 3–0 during the 1995–96 <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League Cup">League Cup</a>. Their matches are played at <a href="/wiki/Bootham_Crescent" title="Bootham Crescent">Bootham Crescent</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>York also has a strong <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a> history. York FC, later known as <a href="/wiki/York_City_Knights" title="York City Knights">York Wasps</a>, formed in 1901, were one of the oldest rugby league clubs in the country but the effects of a move to the out of town <a href="/wiki/Huntington_Stadium" title="Huntington Stadium">Huntington Stadium</a>, poor results and falling attendances led to their bankruptcy in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> The supporters formed a new club, <a href="/wiki/York_City_Knights" title="York City Knights">York City Knights</a>, who now play at the same stadium in <a href="/wiki/Championship_1" class="mw-redirect" title="Championship 1">Championship 1</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> There are three amateur rugby league teams in York; New Earswick All Blacks (in <a href="/wiki/New_Earswick" title="New Earswick">New Earswick</a>), York Acorn and <a href="/wiki/Heworth_A.R.L.F.C." title="Heworth A.R.L.F.C.">Heworth</a>. <a href="/wiki/York_International_9s" title="York International 9s">York International 9s</a> was an annual <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league_nines" title="Rugby league nines">rugby league nines</a> tournament which took place in York between 2002 and 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup>
Amateur side <a href="/wiki/York_Lokomotive" title="York Lokomotive">York Lokomotive</a> compete in the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_Conference" title="Rugby League Conference">Rugby League Conference</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:York_City_RC_Boathouse.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/York_City_RC_Boathouse.jpg/220px-York_City_RC_Boathouse.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/York_City_RC_Boathouse.jpg/330px-York_City_RC_Boathouse.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/York_City_RC_Boathouse.jpg/440px-York_City_RC_Boathouse.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:York_City_RC_Boathouse.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/York_City_Rowing_Club" title="York City Rowing Club">York City Rowing Club</a></div></div></div>
<p>An open rowing club <a href="/wiki/York_City_Rowing_Club" title="York City Rowing Club">York City Rowing Club</a> is located underneath Lendal Bridge.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> The rowing clubs of The University of York, <a href="/wiki/York_St_John_University_Rowing_Club" title="York St John University Rowing Club">York St John University Rowing Club</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leeds_University_Boat_Club" title="Leeds University Boat Club">Leeds University Boat Club</a> as well as York City RC use the Ouse for training. There are two sailing clubs close to York, both of which sail dinghies on the River Ouse. The York RI (Railway Institute) Sailing Club has a club house and boat park on the outskirts of <a href="/wiki/Bishopthorpe" title="Bishopthorpe">Bishopthorpe</a>, a village 3 miles (4.8&#160;km) to the south of York. The Yorkshire Ouse Sailing Club has a club house in the village of <a href="/wiki/Naburn" title="Naburn">Naburn</a>, 5 miles (8.0&#160;km) south of York.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:York_Racecourse_-_Stands.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/York_Racecourse_-_Stands.jpg/220px-York_Racecourse_-_Stands.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/York_Racecourse_-_Stands.jpg/330px-York_Racecourse_-_Stands.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/York_Racecourse_-_Stands.jpg/440px-York_Racecourse_-_Stands.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2163" data-file-height="1442" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:York_Racecourse_-_Stands.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A view of the stands at <a href="/wiki/York_Racecourse" title="York Racecourse">York Racecourse</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/York_Racecourse" title="York Racecourse">York Racecourse</a> was established in 1731 and from 1990 has been awarded Northern Racecourse of the Year for 17 years running. This major <a href="/wiki/Horseracing" class="mw-redirect" title="Horseracing">horseracing</a> venue is located on the <a href="/wiki/Knavesmire" title="Knavesmire">Knavesmire</a> and sees thousands flocking to the city every year for the 15 race meetings. The Knavesmire Racecourse also hosted <a href="/wiki/Royal_Ascot" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Ascot">Royal Ascot</a> in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> In August racing takes place over the four-day <a href="/wiki/Ebor_Festival" title="Ebor Festival">Ebor Festival</a> that includes the Ebor Handicap dating from 1843.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Motorbike speedway once took place at York. The track in the Burnholme Estate was completed in 1930 and a demonstration event staged. In 1931 the track staged team and open events and the York team took part in the National Trophy.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>York hosts the <a href="/wiki/UK_Championship" title="UK Championship">UK Snooker Championship</a>, which is the second biggest ranking tournament in the sport, at the York Barbican Centre.
</p><p>On 6 July 2014, York hosted the start of Stage 2 of the 2014 <a href="/wiki/Tour_de_France" title="Tour de France">Tour de France</a>. Starting the Départ Fictif from <a href="/wiki/York_Racecourse" title="York Racecourse">York Racecourse</a>, the riders travelled through the city centre to the Départ Actuel on the A59 just beyond the junction with the Outer Ring Road heading towards <a href="/wiki/Knaresborough" title="Knaresborough">Knaresborough</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, the inaugural <a href="/wiki/Tour_de_Yorkshire" title="Tour de Yorkshire">Tour de Yorkshire</a> was held as a legacy event to build on the popularity of the previous year, with the Day 2 stage finishing in York.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The most notable sportsmen to come from York in recent years are footballers <a href="/wiki/Lucy_Staniforth" title="Lucy Staniforth">Lucy Staniforth</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/2017_FIFA_U-20_World_Cup" title="2017 FIFA U-20 World Cup">Under-20 World Cup</a> winning captain <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Cook_(footballer,_born_1997)" title="Lewis Cook (footballer, born 1997)">Lewis Cook</a><sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> and former <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> manager <a href="/wiki/Steve_McClaren" title="Steve McClaren">Steve McClaren</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geodesy">Geodesy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Geodesy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/York_Minster" title="York Minster">York Minster</a> was the origin (meridian) of the 6 inch and 1:2500 Ordnance Survey maps for Yorkshire.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="Twin_towns_.E2.80.93_sister_cities"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_–_sister_cities">Twin towns – sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=York&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Twin towns – sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in the United Kingdom">List of twin towns and sister cities in the United Kingdom</a></div>
<table class="wikitable">

<tbody><tr valign="top">
<td>York is <a href="/wiki/Twin_towns_and_sister_cities" class="mw-redirect" title="Twin towns and sister cities">twinned</a> with:
<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/France" title="France"><img alt="France" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/23px-Flag_of_France.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/35px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/45px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Dijon" title="Dijon">Dijon</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, since 1953<sup id="cite_ref-Twin_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Twin-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany"><img alt="Germany" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/23px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/35px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/46px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCnster" title="Münster">Münster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, since 1957<sup id="cite_ref-Twin_227-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Twin-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Münster_twinnings_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Münster_twinnings-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/China" title="China"><img alt="China" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Nanjing" title="Nanjing">Nanjing</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, since 2016<sup id="cite_ref-York_Press_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-York_Press-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Visit_York_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Visit_York-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>On 22 October 2014, it announced the first 'temporal twinning' with Jórvík, the Viking city on the site of York from 866 to 1066.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
